Distinguishing Correctness and Consideration in Book Openings
Author examines validity and consideration of book-opening modes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between correctness (sihha) and consideration (i'tibar) in evaluating modes of opening a scholarly work, and apply the criteria of real beginning and unity of type to determine which modes are considered.

Core Idea
Correctness is necessary but not sufficient; a mode must also align with customary practice to be considered.

When scholars evaluate how to open a book with basmala and hamd, they do not simply ask 'Is this correct?' but also 'Is this considered (mu'tabar) in the tradition?' This passage from a hashiya on a standard theological text breaks down the various possible faces (wujuh) of opening, classifying them as correct or not, and considered or not. You will learn the two principles that determine correctness—real beginning (al-ibtida' al-haqiqi) and unity of type (ittihad naw' al-ibtida')—and how custom ('urf) elevates a correct mode to a considered one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two principles of a correct opening
The author refers to 'the two principles': the beginning being real (haqiqi) and the unity of the type of beginning. Look for where he mentions 'كون الابتداء حقيقياً' and 'اتحاد نوع الابتداء'.
These principles ensure the opening is genuine and consistent.
2
Classify the six faces into correct and non-correct
Based on these principles, the first two faces are correct and considered; the last three are correct but not considered because they lack the two principles. The first non-considered face is ambiguous.
Correctness alone does not guarantee consideration.
3
Distinguish correctness from consideration
The author states: 'كون الشيء معتبراً أو غير معتبر إنما هو بعد كونه صحيحاً' – a thing is only considered after it is correct. So consideration is a further condition.
Not everything correct is automatically mu'tabar.
4
Apply the role of custom ('urf)
The passage explains that the determination of what is correct and considered depends on the current custom of placing basmala before hamd. Without that custom, the faces would change.
Custom is the final arbiter of consideration.
5
Examine the proposed answer and its critique
The author presents a potential answer that redefines hamd to include basmala, but then critiques it as against apparent meaning and customary usage.
This shows how logical consistency must mesh with linguistic reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في خطبة الكتاب
الثلاثة. ووجه الصحة وعدمها يظهر بما قدمناه فالمحتاج الى البيان وجه الاعتبار و عدمه.
فنقول: أما وجه عدم الاعتبار في الاخيرين من الوجوه الغير المعتبرة فهو خلوهما من الاصلين، كون الابتداء حقيقياً كما فى الوجهين الأولين من الوجوه الصحيحة المعتبرة و اتحاد نوع الابتداء كما في الوجه الاخير منها.
و اما وجه عدم الاعتبار في الأول من الوجوه الغير المعتبرة ففيه خفاء لاشتماله على الاصل الثاني ضرورة فاما ان يعتبر هذا ايضاً اولم يعتبر الوجه الاخير من الوجوه المعتبرة ايضاً، فالفرق تحكم اللهم الا ان يقال : ان الحمل على العرفى كثير شايع عندهم بخلاف الاضافى فتأمل.
ثم لا يخفى ان كون الشيء معتبراً أو غير معتبر انما هو بعد كونه صحيحاً فلا يرد ان واحداً من الوجوه لا لغائه معاً فلا الثلاثة الأخيرة لا محالة مشتمل على الأصلين عن درجة الاعتبار هذا.
وجه
و اعلم ان تعيين الصحيح وغيره والمعتبر وغيره على الوجه المذكور انما هو على العادة المعمولة الأن من تقديم البسملة على الحمد والا لاختلف الوجوه صحة واعتباراً وعدمهما قرب وجه صحيح على الاول غير صحيح عليه وهكذا فعليك بالتأمل لئلا يختلط عليك الحال .
و قد يجاب ايضاً عن اصل الاشكال بانّ المراد من الحمد اظهار صفاته الجميلة سواء كان بلفظ الحمد ام لا ففى التسمية جهة التحميد فاذا ابتدأ بها يحصل الامتثال بكلا الخيرين. وبان: الحديثين انما وردا على سبيل منع الحلو، بمعنى ان كل امرذى بال لم يبدء بواحد من البسملة والحمد فهواية ، فيكفى الابتداء باحدهما فقط ابتداء حقيقياً لكن الأولى ان يبتدء بالبسملة لاشتمالها على التحميد ايضاً كما ذكر و لما فيه من الاشارة الى ان الافعال انما تحصل بمعونة اسمه الأعظم.
ولا يخفى ما فيها من ارتكاب خلاف الظاهر اما فى الثانى فظاهر و اما في الاول، فلان احكام الشارع انما هو منزل على الامور العرفية ولا يقال فى العرف لمن اتى بالبسملة : انه حمد ولذا لم يتعرض اليهما المحشى (ره) (میرزا محمد علی (ره)
In the sermon of the book: The three. And the aspect of correctness and its lack appears from what we have presented, so what needs explanation is the aspect of consideration and its lack. So we say: As for the aspect of lack of consideration in the last two of the non-considered faces, it is their being devoid of the two [original] principles, [namely] that the beginning is real as in the first two of the correct considered faces, and the unity of the type of beginning as in the last of them. And as for the aspect of lack of consideration in the first of the non-considered faces, there is obscurity in it because of its inclusion of the second principle necessarily; so either this [principle] is also considered or the last of the considered faces is also not considered, so the difference is arbitrary unless it is said: The application to the customary is frequent and common among them unlike the additive, so reflect. Then it is not hidden that a thing being considered or not is only after it is correct, so it is not objected that one of the faces is not vain at all; so the last three necessarily include the two principles, [falling] from the degree of consideration. This is an aspect. And know that the determination of the correct and its other, and the considered and its other, in the mentioned manner, is only according to the current custom of placing the basmala before the hamd; otherwise the faces would differ in correctness and consideration and their lack: a face correct according to the first is not correct according to it, and so on. So upon you is reflection so that the situation does not become confused for you. And it may also be answered regarding the original difficulty: that what is meant by hamd is the manifestation of His beautiful attributes, whether by the word al-hamd or not; so in the tasmiya there is an aspect of tahmid. So if one begins with it, compliance with both goods is achieved. And by [the claim] that the two hadiths were only reported by way of prohibition of honey [؟] meaning that every important matter that does not begin with one of the basmala and hamd is deficient; so beginning with only one of them suffices as a real beginning, but it is preferable to begin with the basmala because it includes tahmid as mentioned, and because of the indication that actions are only achieved with the help of His greatest name. And it is not hidden what is in these [responses] of violation of the apparent meaning; as for the second, it is apparent, and as for the first, because the rulings of the Lawgiver are indeed based on customary matters, and it is not said in custom of one who comes with the basmala that he has done hamd, and therefore the commentator (Mirza Muhammad Ali) did not address them.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement, typical of a hashiya, where the super-commentator analyzes the validity and consideration of various ways to open a book with the basmala and hamd. The author begins by referring to a previous discussion of 'three' faces, then states that what needs explanation is the aspect of consideration (i'tibar) versus non-consideration. He enumerates the non-considered faces: the last two lack the two principles (real beginning and unity of type), while the first non-considered face is obscure because it includes the second principle. He suggests that the difference between considering and not considering that face is arbitrary unless one invokes customary usage (al-'urfi) versus additive (al-idafi). Then he notes that consideration presupposes correctness, so the last three faces, though correct, fall from consideration because they include the two principles. Next, he explains that the determination of correct and considered depends on the current custom of placing basmala before hamd. He then presents a possible answer to the original difficulty: that hamd means manifesting beautiful attributes regardless of the word, so the basmala contains an aspect of tahmid, and two hadiths about beginning with basmala or hamd are interpreted as prohibiting only the omission of both, so beginning with one suffices. However, he immediately critiques this answer as violating the apparent meaning, because in custom, saying the basmala is not called hamd, and therefore the commentator Mirza Muhammad Ali avoided this response. This demonstrates the scholar's careful weighing of logical and customary considerations.

Using 'من' to Signal the Perfect Individual
Commentator explains the mystic maxim and the rhetorical nuance of using the indefinite 'من' for the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the rhetorical device of using an indefinite relative pronoun to indicate the perfect individual in Islamic texts.

Core Idea
The indefinite 'من' can highlight that the referent is the perfect exemplar of its kind.

In this passage, the commentator Abdurrahim unpacks a subtle rhetorical choice: why the author uses the indefinite 'من' (who) instead of naming the Prophet explicitly. Understanding this device deepens your appreciation of how scholars convey profound meanings through linguistic precision – a skill essential for interpreting Islamic texts with nuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mystic maxim
Find the saying 'خذوا الغايات واتركوا المبادىء' (Take the ends and leave the beginnings). This is the starting point for the commentary.
The maxim is from 'ahl al-‘irfān' (people of gnosis).
2
Recognize the rhetorical shift
Notice that the author refers to the Prophet using the indefinite 'من' rather than explicitly naming him. This is a deliberate choice, not grammatical accident.
The commentator calls this a 'nukta' (subtle point).
3
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains that using the general term indicates that the Prophet is 'al-fard al-kāmil' (the perfect individual) of humanity. The general pronoun points to a specific individual because he perfectly embodies the genus.
The mind immediately leaps from the general term to the Prophet because he is the complete exemplar.
4
Connect to broader Islamic teachings
The commentator reinforces this by mentioning that the Prophet is the cause of the world's existence and that even angels prostrated to Adam, implying the Prophet's ultimate status.
This shows the theological grounding of the rhetorical choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في خطبة الكتاب و هذا معنى قول اهل العرفان: خذوا الغايات واتركوا المبادى». (عبدالرحيم) (۵۱) قوله تعظيماً واجلالاً: نكتة لمجرد عدم التصريح و اما نكتة التعبير عن الحضرة المحمدية صلى الله عليه و آله بكلمة «من» الابهامية هى الاشارة الى انه الفرد الكامل لهذا الجنس. وكانه اطلق العام واراد به الخاص تنبيهاً على ان هذا الخاص هو الفرد الكامل بحيث لا يتبادر الذهن منه الا اليه و كيف لا يكون كذلك ؟ و هو السبب لوجود العالم ولتعظيمه أمير الملائكة ان يسجدوا لادم (ع) كما يدل عليه الاخبار. (عبدالرحيم)
Regarding the introduction of the book: This is the meaning of the saying of the people of gnosis: 'Take the ends and leave the beginnings.' (by Abdurrahim) (51) His statement: 'as an exaltation and veneration': a subtle point for the mere non-explicitness. As for the subtlety of referring to the Prophetic presence, peace be upon him and his family, with the indefinite word 'min', it is an indication that he is the perfect individual of this genus. It is as if he used the general and intended the specific to alert that this specific is the perfect individual such that the mind does not leap from it except to him. How could it not be so? And he is the cause of the existence of the world and for his magnification the chief of the angels prostrated to Adam (AS) as indicated by the traditions. (by Abdurrahim)
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a gloss on the introduction of the book, explaining a saying of the gnostics: 'Take the ends and leave the beginnings.' The commentator Abdurrahim then explains the subtlety (nukta) of why the author did not explicitly name the Prophet but used the indefinite pronoun 'min'. The purpose is to indicate that the Prophet is the perfect individual (fard kamil) of the human genus. By using the general term ('man') and intending the specific (the Prophet), the author alerts the reader that this specific individual is so perfect that the mind immediately turns to him. The commentator supports this by noting that the Prophet is the cause of the world's existence and that even the angels prostrated to Adam, which implies the Prophet's high station.

Key Takeaway
Using a general indefinite term like 'من' can be a rhetorical tool to emphasize that the intended referent is the perfect embodiment of that category.

Why the Attribute of رسالة Was Chosen
Commentator justifies the choice of the attribute 'رسالة' over others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the logical reasoning behind selecting the attribute of رسالة over others based on entailment and explicit mention.

Core Idea
The attribute رسالة entails all perfections and explicitly declares the Prophet's mission.

In this passage, the commentator defends the author's choice of the attribute 'رسالة' (messengership) from the objection that other attributes could also achieve exaltation. He provides two reasons: first, رسالة entails all other perfections (including prophethood and beyond), and second, it explicitly states that the Prophet is a messenger. This is a critical refinement showing how a single attribute can carry multiple significations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the opening: an objector asks why this specific attribute was chosen when others could also exalt. Locate this question in the Arabic.
The question is: 'why did he specify this attribute among all attributes, when that [exaltation] is also attained by them?'
2
Extract the first answer: entailment
The commentator states that رسالة is chosen because it entails all other perfect attributes. Note the phrase 'لِكَوْنِهَا مُسْتَلْزِمَةً لَهَا بِجَمِيعِهَا'.
Entailment means that possessing رسالة necessarily implies possessing other perfections like prophethood, infallibility, etc.
3
Extract the second answer: explicit mention
The second answer is that choosing رسالة already contains an explicit declaration that the Prophet is a messenger. Find the phrase 'مَعَ مَا فِيهِ مِنَ التَّصْرِيحِ بِكَوْنِهِ مُرْسَلًا'.
Other attributes like نبوة would not explicitly convey the mission of bringing a new law.
4
Understand the combined justification
The two reasons work together: رسالة is comprehensive (entailment) and unambiguous (explicit declaration). This justifies its choice over other attributes.
The commentator also notes that the rank of رسالة is above نبوة, so it includes it with an increase.

(۵۲) لما كان لقائل ان يقول اذا كان المقصود من عدم التصريح بالاسم، التعظيم و التنبيه المذكور، فلم خص هذه الصفة من بين سائر الصفات مع انه انما يحصل بها ايضاً كما لا يخفى؟ ، تصدى الى الجواب وقال: و اختار هذه الصفة من بين سائر الصفات لكونها مستلزمة لها بجميعها كما هو ظاهر. و قوله مع ما فيه من التصريح بكونه مرسلاً جواب آخر يعنى ان في اختيار تلك الصفة مع ما ذكر تصريحاً بكونه صلى الله عليه و آله مرسلاً (میرزا محمد علی) (۵۳) قوله لسائر الصفات اى باقى الصفات (والسائر) مشتق من «السور» ای باقي ما يؤكل . (عبد الرحيم) (۵۴) الظاهر انه تعليل لما ذكر فى الجواب الثانى من ان التصريح بكونه مرسلاً علة وسبب لاختيار هذه الصفة من بين ساير الصفات. و يحتمل أن يكون تعليلاً لاستلزام المذكور في الجواب الاول فافهم (محمد علی) (۵۵) قوله فان مرتبة الرسالة فوق النبوة يمكن ان يكون هذا الكلام علة لكل من الوجهين اللذين ذكره في وجه اختيار المصنف صفة الرسالة اما كونه علة للوجه الاول فبان يقال: اختار من بين الصفات هذه ، لكونها مستلزمة لسائر الصفات الكمالية، اما استلزامه صفة النبوة ، فلان الرسالة فوق مرتبة النبوة اى مشتملة على النبوة مع الزيادة اذالمرسل هو النبي الذى ارسل اليه دين وكتاب بخلاف النبي ان يكون له دين وكتاب او يكون تابعاً لدين النبي السابق. فانه اعم من و اما استلزامها صفة غير النبوة كالشجاعة والعصمة فظاهر خصوصاً في نبينا (ص) فان ذاته العالية مستجمعة بجميع الفضائل والكمالات ونعم ما قيل: آنچه خوبان همه دارند تو تنها داری» و لذا لم يلتفت اليه. و اما كونه علة للوجه الثانى فبان يقال: اختار المصنف صفة الرسالة من بين الصفات لان فيها تصريحاً بانه (ص) مرسل بخلاف باقي الصفات. اما صفة النبوة فلان الرسالة فوق النبوة فلا تسلتزمها حتى يكون التصريح بها في قوة التصريح بالرسالة. و اما صفة غير النبوة فظاهر أيضاً لا يحتاج الى البيان. ثم اعلم ان اثبات الفرق بين الرسول والنبى و ان كان حقاً كما ذكره صاحب المدارك في قوله تعالى: و ما ارسلنا قبلك من رسول ولانبي حيث قال هذا دليل بين على ثبوت التغاير بينهما بخلاف ما يقول ا البعض من انهما واحد الا ان الفرق بما يفهم من كلام المحشى بالحديث الذي رواه ابوذر الغفاري و هي ان النبي مأة واربعة وعشرون الفاً و الرسول منهم ثلثماة وثلث عشر و نزل لهم مأة و اربعة كتاب. فالحق في التفرقة على ما روى عن المعصومين عليهم السلام ان يقال: ان الرسول من رأى الملك معاينة و يتكلم به بخلاف النّبي فان النبوة يتحقق بالالهام والرؤيا والسماع بالصوت أيضاً. (شيخ عبد الرحيم)
(52) Since an objector might say: If the intention of not explicitly naming is the aforementioned exaltation and alerting, then why did he specify this attribute among all attributes, when that [exaltation] is also attained by them, as is not hidden? He proceeded to answer and said: And he chose this attribute among all attributes because it entails all of them, as is apparent. And his statement: 'along with what is in it of explicit mention of his being a messenger' is another answer, meaning that in choosing that attribute, along with what was mentioned, is an explicit mention of his being a messenger, peace be upon him and his family. (by Mirza Muhammad Ali) (53) His statement: 'for the other attributes': i.e. the remaining attributes; and 'al-sā'ir' is derived from 'al-sawr', i.e. the remainder of what is eaten. (by Abdurrahim) (54) Apparently it is a justification for what was mentioned in the second answer, that the explicit mention of his being a messenger is the cause and reason for choosing this attribute among other attributes. And it is possible that it is a justification for the entailment mentioned in the first answer, so understand. (by Muhammad Ali) (55) His statement: 'For the rank of messengership is above prophethood': this statement can be a cause for each of the two aspects that he mentioned regarding the author's choice of the attribute of messengership. As for it being a cause for the first aspect, it is said: He chose this among the attributes because it entails all the perfect attributes. As for its entailing the attribute of prophethood, it is because messengership is above the rank of prophethood, i.e. it includes prophethood with an increase, since the messenger is the prophet to whom a religion and a book were revealed, unlike the prophet who may have a religion and a book or be a follower of a previous prophet's religion. For it is more general than that. And as for its entailing other attributes like courage and infallibility, it is apparent, especially in our Prophet (peace be upon him), for his lofty essence encompasses all virtues and perfections. How excellent is what was said: 'What all the good have, you alone have.' Therefore he did not pay attention to it. And as for it being a cause for the second aspect, it is said: The author chose the attribute of messengership among the attributes because in it there is an explicit mention that he (peace be upon him) is a messenger, unlike the other attributes. As for the attribute of prophethood, because messengership is above prophethood, it does not entail it, so that the explicit mention of it would be equivalent to the explicit mention of messengership. And as for other than prophethood, it is also apparent, needing no explanation. Then know that proving the difference between the messenger and the prophet is indeed correct, as the author of al-Madarik mentioned regarding the verse 'And We sent not before you any messenger or prophet' (Qur'an 22:52), where he said this is clear evidence for the existence of a distinction between them, contrary to what some say that they are one. However, the difference as understood from the statement of the commentator (al-muhashshi) based on the hadith narrated by Abu Dharr al-Ghifari is that the number of prophets is one hundred and twenty-four thousand, and the messengers among them are three hundred and thirteen, and one hundred and four books were revealed to them. The correct distinction according to what is narrated from the Infallibles (peace be upon them) is to say that the messenger is one who sees the angel directly and speaks with him, unlike the prophet, for prophethood is realized by inspiration, dreams, and hearing a sound as well. (by Shaykh Abdurrahim)
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement addressing why the author chose the attribute of 'رسالة' (messengership) over other attributes like 'نبوة' (prophethood). The commentator explains that the attribute was chosen because it entails all other perfections and also explicitly states that the Prophet is a messenger. The justification is twofold: first, the rank of messengership is above prophethood, so it includes prophethood and adds the mission of conveying a new law; second, it provides an explicit declaration of his being a messenger. The passage then discusses the distinction between a prophet (نبي) and a messenger (رسول), citing Quranic evidence and a hadith from Abu Dharr al-Ghifari, concluding that a messenger sees the angel directly and speaks with him, while a prophet may receive revelation through inspiration, dreams, or sound.

نبوة

Why did the commentator say that رسالة entails other attributes?

B) Because it is the highest rank.
C) Because it includes all other perfect attributes due to being above them.
D) Because the author said so.

Key Takeaway
The attribute رسالة was chosen because it entails all perfections and explicitly declares the Prophet's mission.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Distinction Between Nabi and Rasul
Commentator clarifies the distinction between prophet and messenger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a prophet (نبي) and a messenger (رسول) according to the theological arguments presented in the passage.

Core Idea
A messenger is a prophet with direct angelic communication and a new law; a prophet may receive revelation indirectly.

This part of the passage resolves a theological debate: are prophet and messenger the same? The commentator cites Quranic evidence and a hadith to argue that they are distinct, with الرسول being a higher rank that includes النبوة and adds direct angelic encounter and a new scripture. The key criterion is the mode of revelation: a messenger sees the angel directly and speaks with him, while a prophet may receive through inspiration, dreams, or sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing views
Find in the passage where it says 'خلاف ما يقول بعض من انهما واحد' (contrary to what some say they are one). This sets up the debate.
The passage sides with the majority view that they are distinct.
2
Locate the Quranic evidence
The commentator references Quran 22:52: 'وما أرسلنا من قبلك من رسول ولا نبي' (And We sent not before you any messenger or prophet). Note how this verse juxtaposes the two terms.
This is taken as evidence that they are not identical, otherwise the pairing would be redundant.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
A hadith from Abu Dharr al-Ghifari gives numbers: 124,000 prophets, 313 messengers, with 104 books. This quantitative difference supports distinction.
Messengers are a subset of prophets, but not all prophets are messengers.
4
Extract the defining criterion
The passage concludes: 'الرسول من رأى الملك معاينة ويتكلم به' (the messenger sees the angel directly and speaks with him), while the prophet receives by inspiration, dreams, or sound.
This criterion is based on narrations from the Infallibles.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Metaphorical Use of المصدر as الحال in Arabic Logical Texts
Commentators discuss the grammatical status of 'هدى' and metaphorical solutions for abstract nouns as hāl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a masdar is used metaphorically as a hāl and distinguish between metaphorical word usage and metaphorical attribution in Arabic logical texts.

Core Idea
An abstract noun as a circumstantial accusative requires metaphorical interpretation – either in the word or in the attribution.

In the khutbah of the book, the word 'هدى' (guidance) appears. Commentators analyze its grammatical status: is it a verbal noun (masdar) acting as an active participle? Is it a circumstantial accusative (hāl) from the agent or object? This lesson unpacks the principle that an abstract noun cannot directly be a hāl for a concrete noun; it must be interpreted metaphorically. This principle applies widely in Arabic logical and theological prose, ensuring precise comprehension of definitions and arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical problem
Locate the word 'هدى' in the khutbah and note its apparent function as a hāl. Consider why this is problematic: a hāl must be a concrete description, but 'هدى' is an abstract verbal noun.
The passage discusses whether 'هدى' is a masdar in the meaning of an active participle (هادٍ) or used hyperbolically.
2
Understand the condition for hāl
Recall that a hāl requires unity in existence (ittiḥād fī al-wujūd) with the noun it describes. An abstract noun (ism ma‘nā) differs in existence from a concrete noun (ism ‘ayn), so direct use is impossible.
This is a well-established grammatical rule, as mentioned by the commentators.
3
Analyze the two metaphorical solutions
The commentators propose two types of tajawwuz: (1) metaphorical word usage (tajawwuz fī al-kalima) – the masdar is interpreted as an active/passive participle; (2) metaphorical attribution (tajawwuz fī al-isnād) – the masdar remains but is attributed metaphorically. Distinguish between them.
A third possibility, metaphor by omission (majāz al-ḥadhf), is also mentioned but not fully explained.
4
Apply to the example of 'Zayd is justice'
Consider the statement 'Zaydun ‘adlun' (Zayd is justice). Analyze how it illustrates both possibilities: either 'adlun' is used in the meaning of 'just' (ism fā‘il), or the attribution is metaphorical (justice attributed to Zayd).
The passage notes that the latter interpretation is more apparent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۶) قيل هو مصدر بمعنى اسم الفاعل والظاهر أنه اسم للحاصل بالمصدر اطلق عليه مبالغة و :قوله به الاقتداء مبنى المفعول اى بان یقتدی ،به قوله «به» متعلق بالاقتداء ولا يليق تعلقه بيليق فافهم (جلال الدين) (۵۷) قوله و حینئذ اى وحين اذ جعلناه مفعولا له لقوله «ارسله» لزم ان يراد بالهدی هدی الله حتى يكون المصدر المذكور فعلاً منسوباً تفاعل الفعل الذى هو الارسال المعلل بهذا المصدر، أى علة ارسال الله النبي هو ارادة الله ان يهدى به الناس ولا مانع من ان يراد بالهدى هدى النبي نفسه بمعنى : ارسل الله النبي لاجل ان يهدى الناس إلى الله (التقريب ص ٩) (۵۸) قوله وح يراد بالهدى هدى الله وذلك ، لانه اشتهر بين النحاة ان حذف اللام من المفعول له لا يجوز الا اذا كان فعلاً لفاعل الفعل المعلل بهای بالمفعول به هو الله تعالى فلا بد ان يكون المراد بالهداية هدايته حتى يكون فاعلها متحدين وذهب بعضهم إلى ن الشرط اغلبي لا كلى و هو مرتضى الشيخ محتجاً بقول امير المؤمنين صلوات الله وسلامه عليه و آله في نهج البلاغه: «فاعطاه الله تعالى النظرة استحقاقاً للسخطة و استتماماً للبلية فان فاعل الانظار هو الله تعالى وفاعل الاستحقاق هو ابليس لعنه الله. قال لا يجوز جعل استحقاقاً» حالا من الفعل لان «استتماماً» ح حال من الفاعل ويمتنع حال احدهما على حال الآخر. عطف قال صاحب البهجة لا يجوز ايضاً جعل الأول حالاً و الثاني مفعولاً له لوجود العاطف. . نعم يمكن من المفعول باسناد الاستتمام اليه مجازاً للسببية او تأويله بتقدير الارادة كما قالوا في قوله جمله حالاً تعالى يريكم البرق خوفاً و طمعاً أى ارادة خوفكم و طمعكم . (عبدالرحيم) (۵۹) قوله او حال عن الفاعل اى فاعل ،ارسله و هو الضمير المستتر الراجع الى الله تعالى. فيكون المعنى ارسل الله النبي حال كونه (هادياً وقوله : بل عن المفعول به، الضمير في «به» راجع الى «ال» الموصولة فى المفعول اى الذي فعل به الفعل. وفي كلمة بل اشارة إلى كونه حالاً من المفعول به هو الانسب بقرينة قوله : هو بالاهتداء حقيق و نوراً به الاقتداء يليق فانها مناسبان للمفعول كما لا يخفى لذوى العقول . (عبد الرحيم) (۶۰) قوله وح فالمصدر: يعنى على فالمصدر: يعني على تقدير كون الهدى حالاً سواء كان عن الفاعل أو المفعول فهو اما بمعنى اسم الفاعل او الاطلاق على سبيل المبالغة بيان ذلك انهم ذكروا انه لا يجوز كون اسم المعنى خبراً أو حالاً أو صفة لاسم العين لان كلامنها يستدعى الاتحاد في الوجود مع ما هو له ولاشك في تغاير المعنى والعين فكل ما يتوهم في الظاهر انه من هذا القبيل فبنى على التجوز اما في الكلمة أو الاسناد اما الاول فبأن يقال: المراد من المصدر هو اسم الفاعل أو المفعول حيث يقتضيه المقام مجازاً واما الثاني فبان يقال انه باق على حاله لكنه اسند الى الفاعل أو المفعول على سبيل التجوز في الاسناد فح يحتمل ان يكون المراد بقوله : «نحوزيد عدل بيان النظير لكلا الامرين وان كان الظهور في الاخير فقط . ثم انه لا يخفى انه يمكن فى امثال ما نحن فيه توجيه ثالث و هو ان يكون من باب المجاز فى الحذف بناء
(56) It is said that it is a verbal noun (masdar) in the meaning of the active participle (ism al-fā‘il), and apparently it is a name for the product of the masdar, used hyperbolically. And his statement: 'to him the following' is based on the object [passive] structure, i.e. that he is followed. His statement 'to him' is related to 'following' and it is not appropriate to relate it to 'be appropriate', so understand. (by Jalal al-Din) (57) His statement: 'and then' i.e. when we made it an object of purpose (maf‘ūl lahu) for his statement 'He sent him', it is necessary that by 'guidance' (al-huda) is meant the guidance of Allah, so that the mentioned masdar becomes an attributive action to the action of sending that is justified by this masdar. That is, the cause of Allah sending the prophet is Allah's will to guide people through him. And there is no obstacle to meaning by 'guidance' the prophet's own guidance, i.e., Allah sent the prophet so that he guides people to Allah. (from al-Taqrib, p. 9) (58) His statement: 'and then it is intended by guidance the guidance of Allah' – and that is because it is well-known among grammarians that the omission of 'lam' (li-) from the object of purpose is not permissible unless the action is attributed to the agent of the verb that is being justified by it. Since the verb 'He sent' is attributed to Allah, and the agent of the object of purpose (the guidance) must be the same, so the guidance must be His guidance so that the agent is unified. Some scholars held that this condition is predominant, not universal, and this is the view endorsed by the Shaykh, citing the statement of Amir al-Mu'minin (peace be upon him) in Nahj al-Balaghah: 'Thus Allah gave him respite, deserving of wrath and completion of trial.' For the agent of 'giving respite' (al-inzār) is Allah, while the agent of 'deserving' (al-istihqāq) is Iblis (may Allah curse him). He said: It is not permissible to make 'deserving' a circumstantial accusative (hāl) from the verb, because 'completion' is a hāl from the agent, and it is impossible for one of them to be a hāl of the other. 'Atf' – the author of al-Bahjah said: It is also not permissible to make the first a hāl and the second an object of purpose because of the conjunction. However, it is possible to make it an object of purpose by attributing 'completion' to it metaphorically as a cause, or by interpreting it with the appreciation of 'will', as they said regarding His statement (exalted) 'He shows you the lightning, fear and hope' – i.e., willing your fear and hope. (by Abdurrahim) (59) His statement 'or a hāl from the agent' – i.e., the agent of 'He sent him' is the implicit pronoun referring to Allah. Thus the meaning would be: Allah sent the prophet while he (the prophet) is a guide. And his statement 'rather from the object' – the pronoun in 'to him' refers to the relative pronoun 'al-', i.e., the one who did the action. And the word 'rather' indicates that it being a hāl from the object is more appropriate, by the indication of his statement: 'he is worthy of guidance and a light, following him is appropriate', for these are more suitable for the object, as is not hidden from those of intellect. (by Abdurrahim) (60) His statement 'then the masdar' – i.e., on the assumption that 'guidance' is a hāl, whether it is from the agent or the object, it is either in the meaning of the active participle or is used hyperbolically. The explanation is that they mentioned that it is not permissible for an abstract noun (ism ma‘nā) to be a predicate (khabar), a hāl, or an adjective for a concrete noun (ism ‘ayn), because each of them requires unity in existence with what it is for, and there is no doubt about the difference between the abstract and the concrete. So whatever appears externally to be of this type is based on metaphor (tajawwuz), either in the word or in the attribution (isnād). As for the first, it is said that what is meant by the masdar is the active or passive participle as the context requires, metaphorically. As for the second, it is said that it remains as it is but is attributed to the agent or object by way of metaphorical attribution. Then it is possible that what is meant by his statement 'Zayd is justice' is an example of both possibilities, although the apparent one is only the latter. Then it is not hidden that in cases like ours a third interpretation is possible, namely that it is a case of metaphor by omission (majāz al-hadhr), based on...
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage comprises grammatical glosses on the khutbah (introduction) of the book, focusing on the word 'هدى' (guidance) and its syntactic function. The commentators discuss whether 'هدى' is a masdar acting as an active participle, and whether it is a circumstantial accusative (hāl) from the agent or object. They delve into the rules for omitting the 'lam' from the object of purpose (maf‘ūl lahu), citing Nahj al-Balaghah as a counterexample to the rule that the agent must be the same. The discussion then extends to the general principle that abstract nouns cannot directly be predicates or hāl of concrete nouns without metaphorical interpretation, and propose two solutions: either the masdar is used figuratively as an active/passive participle, or the attribution (isnād) is metaphorical. A third possibility of metaphor by omission is also suggested.

Abstract nouns as circumstantial accusatives require metaphorical interpretation – either the word is taken in a concrete sense or the attribution is metaphorical.

Introduction and Front Matter

Why 'Adl' Cannot Be a Hal for Allah
Author explains why 'adl' cannot be a hal for Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why a circumstantial (hal) interpretation of a divine attribute is theologically invalid and distinguish the two readings of 'al-mursal'.

Core Idea
A grammatical form implying change cannot describe the Unchanging.

In the preface of many Islamic books, the phrase 'al-'adl' (the Just) appears. A grammatical nuance arises: should we read it as a circumstantial state (hal) describing a temporary condition, or as an inherent quality? This lesson unpacks the theological reasoning that forces the latter interpretation when the subject is Allah, and clarifies a similar point for the word 'al-mursal'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two grammatical possibilities for 'adl'
The word 'adl' in the sentence 'Zayd 'adl' can be interpreted either as a circumstantial state (hal: 'Zayd being just') or as a predicate meaning 'possessor of justice' (dhū 'adl). Recognize that the hal implies a temporary condition, while the predicate implies a permanent quality.
2
Understand why hal is impermissible for Allah
A hal describes a transitory state. Since Allah's attributes are eternal and unchanging, a hal cannot be attributed to Him. The author rules out the hal interpretation here because the referent of 'al-mursal bi'l-kasr' is Allah Himself, not a state of His.
3
Apply the same logic to 'al-mursal bi'l-fath'
The word 'al-mursal' with fatha refers to the Prophet (s.a.w.). He is the person himself, not a temporary state. Thus, the hal interpretation fails here as well.
4
Reflect on the commentator's oversight
The author notes that the previous commentator (al-Muhashshi) apparently missed this subtlety. Consider how overlooking a theological principle can lead to an invalid grammatical reading.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في خطبة الكتاب على تقدير المضاف اما قبل اسم العين او قبل اسم المعنى. فقولنا: زيد «عدل» مثلا اما على تقدير حال زيد عدل : اوهو ذو عدل، لكن الأول لا يجوز هنا ضرورة ان المرسل بالكسر هو نفسه تعالى لاحاله وشأنه و كذا المرسل بالفتح هو نفسه (ص) لاحاله وشأنه وكانه لهذالم يتوجه اليه المحشى فتأمل. (محمد على)
In the book's preface, regarding the estimation of the genitive construct, either before a substantive noun or before a verbal noun. Our saying: 'Zayd is 'adl' for example is either on the estimation of a hal: 'Zayd is just', or it is 'he is the possessor of justice'. But the first is not permissible here necessarily because the one sent (with kasra) is He Himself, exalted, not His state and affair. And similarly, the one sent (with fatha) is he himself (peace be upon him), not his state and affair. It seems because of this that the commentator (al-Muhashshi) did not pay attention to this, so reflect.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical and theological clarification regarding the interpretation of the word 'adl' (just) in the book's preface. The author discusses the estimation (taqdir) of a genitive construction (mudaf): whether it is before a substantive noun (ism al-ayn) or a verbal noun (ism al-ma'na). The example given is 'Zayd is 'adl' — this can be interpreted either as a circumstantial state (hal), meaning 'Zayd is just' as a temporary condition, or as an ascribed quality, meaning 'he is the possessor of justice' (dhū 'adl). The first interpretation (as a hal) is ruled out here because the referent of 'the one sent' (al-mursal) when read with a kasra (i.e., Allah as the sender) is Allah Himself, not His state or attributes. Similarly, when read with a fatha (i.e., the Prophet as the sent one), it refers to his person, not his states. The author notes that the earlier commentator (al-Muhashshi) overlooked this point, inviting the reader to reflect.

The Reference of 'This' in the Preface
Author explains the different possible references of 'hādhā' depending on timing of preface writing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two possible referents of 'hādhā' in the preface based on the timing of the preface's composition.

Core Idea
The referent of 'this' in a preface depends on whether it was written before or after the book.

When you open a classical Islamic text, you often encounter the phrase 'amma ba'd, this...' (أما بعد، هذا). But what exactly does 'this' refer to? The author of this commentary explains that the answer depends on when the preface was written. If written before the composition, 'this' points to mental entities; if after, it points to the written inscriptions. Understanding this distinction helps you read prefaces with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Notice that the word 'this' (hādhā) in the preface 'amma ba'd, this...' seems to refer to nothing yet written or spoken, because the author has not produced any speech at that point. This creates an apparent ambiguity.
The author states that the speaker/writer has not yet brought forth anything to refer to.
2
Recognize Mental Preparation
Even before writing, the author has his demands (maṭālib) gathered in his mind, ready to emerge. So 'this' can refer to those mental entities—either the specific meanings or the specific words.
The passage says: 'they find their demands gathered in the mind, ready to emerge.'
3
Distinguish the Two Timings
The key distinction is whether the preface was placed before or after the composition. If before, the referent is mental; if after, the referent is the physical inscriptions (nuqūsh) on the page.
The text explicitly contrasts the two scenarios: 'if the preface was placed before the composition... if it was placed after it.'
4
Determine the Referent Accordingly
Use the timing to decide: before composition → 'this' refers to meanings or words in the mind; after composition → 'this' refers to the written inscriptions that symbolize the words and meanings of the finished work.
The final sentence of the passage gives the rule for the after-composition case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من ظاهره فقوله و بعد، فهذا هو على تقدير «اما بعد فهذا وكلمة هذا الجارية من قلم الكاتب أو لسان المتكلم لم يؤنت بها الى كلام حاضر عتيد لان المتكلم والكاتب لم يأتيا بعد بشيء حتى يشيرا اليه بكلمة هذا و لكنها لما جهزا انفسهما لتحرير الكلام أو القاء الخطاب وجدا مطالبهما محشورة في الذهن مهيأة للبروز الى الخارج فاشارا بكلمة هذا الى ما هو مرتب حاضر في الذهن من المعاني المخصوصة المعبر عنها بالفاظ مخصوصة او من تلك الالفاظ الدالة على المعاني المخصوصة الى ان ما هو مرتب حاضر في الذهن تارة يلتفت اليه باعتباره قوالب لمعان او معانى تسبك فى قوالب هذا اذا كان وضع الديباجة قبل التصنيف و اما اذا كان وضعها بعده فكلمة هذا اشارة الى النقوش الرامزة الى الالفاظ القائمة بالمعانى المرادة في التأليف.
From its apparent meaning: his statement 'and after, this' is based on the assumption of 'amma ba'd, this'. The word 'this' coming from the writer's pen or speaker's tongue is not directed to a present prepared speech, because the speaker and writer have not yet produced anything to refer to with the word 'this'. But when they have prepared themselves to write discourse or deliver speech, they find their demands gathered in the mind, ready to emerge into the external. So they refer with the word 'this' to what is arranged and present in the mind: either the specific meanings expressed by specific words, or those words indicating the specific meanings. That which is arranged and present in the mind is sometimes regarded as templates for meanings, or meanings cast into templates. This is if the preface was placed before the composition. But if it was placed after it, then the word 'this' refers to the inscriptions that signify the words standing for the intended meanings in the work.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage explains the ambiguity of the word 'this' (hādhā) in the common preface phrase 'amma ba'd, this...'. The author clarifies that when the preface is written before the composition, the word 'this' refers to mental entities: either the specific meanings intended to be expressed, or the specific words that express them. When the preface is written after the composition, 'this' refers to the written inscriptions (nuqūsh) that symbolize the words and meanings. This distinction is important for understanding how prefaces function in Islamic scholarly works.

Key Terms
الديباجة
النقوش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The specific words in the mind
C) The written inscriptions on the page
D) The readers' understanding

Key Takeaway
The referent of 'hādhā' in a preface is determined by whether the preface was composed before (mental entities) or after (physical inscriptions) the main work.

The Particle 'لما' as a Tool of Commentarial Defense
Author discusses the particle لما, its meaning, and defends its use in the division of the book into logic and kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the commentator's defense of the author's use of 'لما' and evaluate its strength using the rules of jadal.

Core Idea
The particle 'لما' can reveal hidden textual divisions when wielded by a skilled commentator.

At first glance, the particle 'لما' seems like a minor grammatical detail. But in the Islamic commentary tradition, it becomes a powerful tool for defending the coherence of a text. This lesson walks you through how the commentator parses 'لما', addresses an objection, and vindicates the author's division of the book into logic and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two interpretations of 'لما'
The commentator notes that 'لما' can be either a particle (حرف) implying causality, or an adverb (ظرف) implying mere temporal coincidence. Understand how each interpretation affects the connection between the two events.
The commentator does not firmly decide between the two, but the key is that both readings require the second event to occur at the time of the first.
2
Understand the objection against the author
A critic imagines that the author used 'لما' to introduce an example of a division (taqseem) before he had actually performed that division. This is the core of the dialectical attack.
The objection is that the author's speech is out of place (لم يقع في موقعه).
3
Extract the commentator's rebuttal
The commentator points to the author's earlier phrase: 'This is the ultimate refinement of speech in the editing of logic and theology.' This phrase, he argues, is a clear indication that the book is divided into logic and kalam, so the division is implicit. Thus the use of 'لما' is justified.
The commentator's method is to find an implicit division in the text rather than an explicit one.
4
Evaluate the strength of the rebuttal
Consider whether an implicit mention is sufficient for the definite article to be used. The commentator himself notes a potential objection: external 'ahd (prior reference) can exist without explicit mention. But he holds that the author's phrase gives a clear enough indication.
This step requires you to assess whether the commentator's defense holds according to the principles of usul and balaghah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله لما علم ضمناً: كلمة «لما» اما ظرف او حرف بمعنى «اد» ترد لربط مضمون جملة بوجود مضمون جملة اخرى كما اذا قلنا : «لما جاء زيد جاء (عمرو فمعناه عند القائل بالحرفية : ان وجود الاول سبب لوجود الثانى وعند القائل بالظرفية : ان الثانى وجد عند وجود الأول سواء كان بالسببية او بالاتفاق. ثم الغرض من هذا الكلام بيان سبب تنكير المقدمة وتعريف القسمين و حاصله ان التعريف اى ((ال) التعرف شيء على الكلمة لا يرتكب اليه الا لمقتض و المقتضى هيهنا بالنسبة الى القسمين موجود و هو تقدم ذكرهما فلذا عرف القسم الأول اى ادخله «ال») و اما بالنسبة الى المقدمة فلا ولذا نكرها فلايرد انه لا يلزم من انتفاء العهد انتفاء التعريف، لعدم الحصاره انحصاره فيه، لكن لكن يرد ان العهد الخارجى هو الاشارة الى حصة معينة و ان لم يتقدم ذكرها لا لفظاً ولا دلالة. ثم انما قدم المصنف القسم الاول لانه مقدمة موصلة الى القسم الثانى (شيخ) عبدالر. (۱۳۰) قوله « لما علم ضمناً ... اعلم: ان لما هذه تختص بالماضي فتقتضى جملتين وجدت ثانيتهما عند وجود اوليها كقولك لما دعانى اجبته ، و اختلف في انها هل هى حرف او ظرف و الاولون هل هي حرف وجود لوجود او وجوب لوجوب والاخرون هل هى بمعنى حين او اذ ولكل قائل. وعن ابن خروف رد على مدعى الاسمية بجواز لما اكرمتنى امس اكرمتك اليوم لانها اذا قدرت ظرفاً كان عاملها الجواب والفعل الواحد لا يقع في زمنين مختلفين. انه و اجيب بان هذا مثل قوله تعالى ان كنت قلته فقد علمته والشرط لا يكون الا مستقبلاً و لكن المعنى: «ان ثبت انى كنت قلته وكذا هنا المعنى لما ثبت اليوم اكرامك لى امس (كرمتك». ثم الغرض من هذا الكلام دفع ما ربما يتوهم فى هذا المقام ان هذا الكلام من المصنف لم يقع في موقعه كما لا يخفى على المنصف فان مثال ذلك انما يؤتى بعد تقسيم الشيء الى قسمين او اقسام متعددة ولم يجز ذلك من المصنف سابقاً. و حاصل الجواب: منع انه لم يجز من المصنف ذلك ، فانّه و ان لم يصرح بذلك فيما مر لكنه اشار اليه في قوله: فهذا غاية تهذيب الكلام في تحرير المنطق والكلام فان فيه دلالة ظاهرة على كون كتابه على قسمين: المنطق و الكلام فيصح العبارة المذكورة في المقام كما لا يخفى على ذوى الافهام. ثم فرع على هذا التفرقة بين القسم الاول والمقدمة حيث عرف المصنف الاول (اى جعله معرفة بـ «ال») و نكر الاخر (أى لم يجعله معرفة بـ «ال») وقال: «فيصح...» ومنهم من جعل ذلك مقصوداً أصلياً للمحشى من غير تعريض لما ذكرناه. ولا يخفى ان هذا لا يلام قول المحشى لم يجنج الى التصريح بهذا ، بل اللازم ح ان يذكر بدله و بدل المتفرع عليه قولناصح تعريف القسم الأول بصيغة الماضى و بدون الفاء كما لا يخفى على من له دربة باساليب الكلام (میرزا محمد علی)
His saying: 'since it was known implicitly': The word 'لما' is either a zarf (adverb) or a harf (particle) meaning 'إذ' (when), used to connect the content of one sentence to the existence of the content of another sentence, as when we say: 'When Zayd came, 'Amr came.' Its meaning, according to those who say it is a particle, is that the existence of the first is the cause of the existence of the second. According to those who say it is an adverb, the second exists at the existence of the first, whether by causality or by coincidence. Then the purpose of this speech is to explain the reason for making 'the introduction' indefinite and defining the two sections; the summary is that definition (i.e., the definite article) is only used on a word when there is a motive, and the motive here regarding the two sections is present, which is their previous mention. Therefore he defined the first section (i.e., he entered it with 'al') and regarding the introduction he did not, so he left it indefinite. So it is not said that lack of 'ahd (prior mention) does not entail lack of definition, since definition is not limited to it. However, it could be objected that external 'ahd is reference to a specific instance even if it was not previously mentioned explicitly or implicitly. Then the author only preceded the first section because it is a prelude leading to the second section. (Shaykh 'Abd al-Rahim) (130) His saying: 'since it was known implicitly'... Know that this 'لما' is specific to the past tense, so it requires two sentences, the second existing at the existence of the first, as you say: 'When he called me, I answered him.' They differed on whether it is a particle or an adverb. The first group said it is a particle of existence for existence or obligation for obligation. The others said it is in the sense of 'hina' (when) or 'idh' (then). Each has a proponent. Ibn Khurf responded to those who claim it is a noun by the permissibility of: 'Since you honored me yesterday, I honor you today' because if it is taken as an adverb, its operator is the answer, and a single action does not occur in two different times. It was answered that this is like His saying: 'If you said it, then He knows it'—the condition can only be future, but the meaning is: 'If it is established that I said it.' Similarly here, the meaning is: 'Since it is established today that you honored me yesterday, I honor you.' Then the purpose of this speech is to repel what might be imagined in this context: that this speech by the author (i.e., the example mentioned) did not occur in its proper place, as is clear to the impartial person, for such an example is only brought after dividing something into two or more parts, and that had not yet occurred by the author earlier. The summary of the answer is to deny that it had not occurred by the author, for although he did not state it explicitly in what passed, he indicated it in his saying: 'This is the ultimate refinement of speech in the editing of logic and theology'—for this is clear evidence that his book is on two parts: logic and theology. So the mentioned expression is correct in this context, as is clear to those of understanding. Then he subsumed under this the distinction between the first section and the introduction: the author defined the first (i.e., made it definite with 'al') and left the other indefinite. He said: 'So it is correct...' Some considered this to be the original intention of the commentator without allusion to what we mentioned. It is clear that this does not contradict the commentator's statement 'he did not need to make it explicit'; rather, it is necessary that he mentions instead of it and instead of what is subsumed under it our saying: 'He defined the first section with the past tense form and without the fa', as is clear to whoever has practice with styles of speech. (Mirza Muhammad 'Ali)
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refinement discussing the particle 'لما' (lammaa) and defending its use by the original author of the base text. The commentator first defines 'لما' as a word that connects two sentences, indicating that the second occurs at the time of the first, either as a cause or coincidentally, depending on whether it is considered a particle or an adverb. He then explains that the author's purpose in using 'لما' was to justify why he made 'the introduction' indefinite and defined the two sections (logic and theology). The author's usage shows that the two sections were previously mentioned, hence they are definite, while the introduction is indefinite. A potential criticism is raised: that the author used 'لما' to introduce an example (of dividing the book) before actually making a division. The commentator rebuts this by pointing to the author's own statement: 'This is the ultimate refinement of speech in the editing of logic and theology,' which implicitly divides the book into logic and theology. Therefore, the use of 'لما' is appropriate. He further subsumes that the author defined the first section (logic) with the definite article and left the introduction indefinite. Some commentators mistakenly think this was the main intention. The text ends with a methodological note about stylistic awareness. This lesson demonstrates the careful attention to wording and context in Islamic logical works.

Why Logic Comes Before Theology
Gloss on the division of the book into two sections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rationale for placing logic before theology in classical Islamic textbooks and identify the two main divisions of knowledge in the book.

Core Idea
Logic is the tool; theology is the goal.

This brief gloss states something that seemed obvious to the commentator: the book has two clear sections, logic and theology. But why is that division worth noting? In the Islamic tradition, logic (mantiq) is not studied for its own sake—it is the instrument (āla) that protects the mind from error when reasoning about sacred matters. Theologians (mutakallimūn) rely on logical principles to defend creedal truths. Therefore, many textbooks begin with logic as a prerequisite. This lesson unpacks the significance of that arrangement.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Two Parts
Read the Arabic: the gloss explicitly says 'his book is divided into two parts: on logic and on theology.' Identify the two disciplines mentioned.
Logic = al-mantiq; Theology = al-kalām.
2
Understand the Glossator's Point
The glossator says the author 'did not need to explicitly state this.' Why? Because the division is obvious from the content. But by mentioning it, the glossator reinforces that the reader should notice the structure.
3
Connect to the Purpose of Logic
Reflect: in the Islamic sciences, logic is considered a tool for valid reasoning. Theology uses that tool to construct arguments about God, prophecy, and the afterlife. So the order—logic first, theology second—is pedagogical: learn the tool before applying it.
This mirrors the common curriculum where mantiq precedes kalām.

Refining the Definition of 'Muqaddima' and Grammatical Objections
Author refines the definition of 'muqaddima' and responds to grammatical objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the grammatical objection against predicating an indefinite noun and evaluate the three responses using the principle of benefit.

Core Idea
An indefinite noun can be predicated if it conveys benefit, not just through artificial specializations.

In logic texts, the opening phrase 'hadhihi muqaddima' (this is a preface) seems straightforward, but grammarians objected that 'muqaddima' is indefinite and cannot be a predicate. This lesson examines how scholars defended it, revealing a deeper principle about when predication is valid. You will learn to recognize and apply the benefit criterion, a key tool in assessing logical definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical structure
The sentence 'hadhihi muqaddima' can be parsed as subject-predicate or inverted. The author notes that some treat 'muqaddima' as predicate of an omitted subject, while others treat it as subject with omitted predicate.
The default rule for subject and predicate is that both should be definite, but exceptions exist.
2
Understand the objection
An indefinite noun (nakira) normally cannot be a predicate because it lacks specificity. The objector says 'muqaddima' is a pure indefinite, so predication is invalid.
3
Analyze the three responses
First response: the tanwin on 'muqaddima' indicates glorification or minimization, making it specific. Second: the predicate is actually a prepositional phrase placed before the indefinite, creating an inverted construction. Third: predication is valid if it conveys benefit (fa'ida), regardless of definiteness.
The third response is considered the strongest by many scholars.
4
Apply the benefit principle
Using the benefit criterion, sentences like 'a tree prostrated' (informative) are permissible, while 'a man standing' (trivial) are not. Practice distinguishing between permissible and impermissible indefinite predications.
This principle is used in later logical and grammatical texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: أي هذه مقدمة: يعني أنها خبر مبتدأ محذوف جرياً على مقتضى الأصل في كل من المبتدأ والخبر ومنهم من جعله مبتدأ محذوف الخبر أي المقدمة في رسم المنطق والحاجة إليه وموضوعه. وأورد عليه: أن قوله «مقدمة» نكرة محضة لا يصح أن يخبر عنها. وأجيب بوجوه، منها: أنه مخصوصة بجعل التنوين فيها للتعظيم أو التقليل، والأول ناظر إلى كثرة فوائدها ووفور عوائدها والثاني إلى قلة ألفاظها وإيجاز كلماتها. ومنها: أنها يقدر الخبر المحذوف قبلها أي في رسم المنطق والحاجة إليه وموضوعه مقدمة فهو نظير قولك: «في الدار رجل». ومنها أن ذلك مبني على ما ذكره جمع من المحققين من أن مدار صحة الإخبار عن النكرة على الفائدة لا على ما ذكروه من التخصيصات التي يحتاج في توجيهاتها إلى الاعتبارات الركيكة والتكلفات الواهية فعلى هذا يجوز «شجرة سجدت» و«كوكب انقض الساعة» وأمثالهما ولا يجوز «رجل قائم» ونظائره. هذا.
His statement: 'This is a preface' means it is the predicate of an omitted subject, proceeding according to the default rule for both subject and predicate. Some have made it a subject with omitted predicate, i.e., 'the preface concerning the definition of logic, the need for it, and its subject.' An objection was raised: that his statement 'preface' is a pure indefinite noun, so it is not valid to predicate of it. It was answered by several points: among them, that it is particularized by making the tanwin denote either glorification or minimization; the first refers to the abundance of its benefits and plentiful returns, and the second to the paucity of its words and brevity of its phrases. Among them: that the omitted predicate is posited before it, i.e., 'in the definition of logic, the need for it, and its subject is a preface,' so it is like your saying: 'In the house is a man.' And among them: that this is based on what a group of investigators mentioned, that the basis for the validity of predicating of an indefinite noun is benefit (fa'ida), not the specializations they mentioned which require in their interpretations weak considerations and feeble contrivances. So on this, 'a tree prostrated' and 'a star fell just now' and the like are permissible, while 'a man standing' and its likes are not permissible. This.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the definition of 'muqaddima' (preface/introduction) as used in a logic text. The author begins by interpreting the phrase 'ay hadhihi muqaddima' as 'this is a preface', where 'muqaddima' is the predicate (khabar) of an omitted subject (mubtada'). He notes that some grammarians treat it as the subject with an omitted predicate meaning 'the preface concerning the definition of logic, the need for it, and its subject'. An objection is then raised: the word 'muqaddima' is a pure indefinite noun (nakira), so it cannot validly serve as a predicate according to Arabic grammatical rules. The author provides three responses. First, the tanwin (nunation) on 'muqaddima' indicates glorification (ta'zim) or minimization (taqlil), making it specific enough for predication; glorification points to its many benefits, minimization to its brevity. Second, the omitted predicate is actually placed before the indefinite, as in 'fi al-dari rajul' (in the house is a man), so the construction is inverted. Third, a group of scholars hold that predication of an indefinite is valid as long as it conveys a benefit (fa'ida), without requiring artificial specializations. Thus, sentences like 'a tree prostrated' or 'a star fell just now' (which are informative) are permissible, while 'a man standing' (which gives no new benefit) is not. This demonstrates the interplay between grammatical theory and logical precision in Islamic scholarship.

Key Terms
مقدمة
نكرة
التنوين
الفائدة

Key Takeaway
The validity of predicating an indefinite noun depends on communicative benefit (fa'ida), not on artificial fixes like tanwin.

Indefinite Nouns as Predicates: Three Justifications
Author analyzes the opening statement's grammar and addresses objections about the indefinite noun.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate the three justifications for predicating an indefinite noun in Arabic grammatical/logical discourse.

Core Idea
An indefinite noun can be a predicate if it provides benefit, not just if it is specifically qualified.

The opening of a classical text often carries grammatical and logical nuances. The commentator here defends the phrasing 'Mukaddimah' (a preface) as a predicate of a deleted subject, addressing objections about its indefiniteness. The three answers illustrate different approaches: reliance on specification via tanwin, reordering the sentence structure, and the more fundamental criterion of benefit (fa'idah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical structure
Recognize that 'Mukaddimah' is treated as a predicate (khabar) of a deleted subject (mubtada' mahdhuf). This is a standard grammatical move in Arabic to provide a concise opening.
The alternative view makes it a subject with a deleted predicate.
2
Understand the objection
The objection states that 'Mukaddimah' is an indefinite noun (nakira), and normally an indefinite noun cannot be a predicate without specification (takhsis). Grasp why this is a problem in Arabic grammar.
Indefinite nouns generally refer to unspecified individuals, making predication ambiguous.
3
Analyze the first answer: specification via tanwin
The tanwin (nunation) on 'Mukaddimah' is not just for indefiniteness but can indicate glorification (ta'zim) or belittlement (taqlil). Here it signifies either the abundance of benefits or the conciseness of words, making the noun specific enough for predication.
This answer relies on morphological nuance.
4
Analyze the second answer: estimated predicate before it
Estimate a deleted predicate before 'Mukaddimah', turning the phrase into 'concerning the definition of logic, the need for it, and its subject matter is a preface'. This makes the indefinite noun part of a quasi-sentence (shibh jumla), like 'fi al-dari rajul' (in the house is a man), where the indefinite is permitted as a predicate of a locative.
This answer reinterprets the sentence structure.
5
Analyze the third answer: benefit (fa'idah) as criterion
According to a group of verifiers (muhaddiqin), the permissibility of an indefinite predicate depends on whether it provides beneficial information (fa'idah), not on arbitrary specifications. For example, 'a tree prostrated' (shajaratun sajadat) is permissible because it conveys a miracle, while 'a man standing' (rajulun qa'imun) is not if the listener already knows men can stand.
This answer shifts the criterion to informativeness, a more logical principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله :ای هذه مقدمة: يعنى انها خير مبتداء محذوف جرياً على مقتضى الأصل في كل من المبتداء والخبر ومنهم من جعله مبتداء محذوف الخبراى المقدمة في رسم المنطق والحاجة اليه وموضوعه. وأورد عليه : ان قوله «مقدمة » نكرة محضة لا يصح ان يخبر عنها . واجيب بوجوه، منها: انه مخصوصة بجعل التنوين فيها للتعظيم أو التقليل، والاول ناظر الى كثرة فوائدها و وفور عوائدها والثانى الى قلة الفاظها و وجازة كلماتها. ومنها : انها يقدر الخبر المحذوف قبلها أى فى رسم المنطق والحاجة اليه وموضوعه مقدمة» فهو نظير قولك: « في الدار رجل». و منها ان ذلك مبنى على ما ذكره جمع من المحققين من ان مدار صحة الاخبار عن النكرة على الفائدة لا على ما ذكروه من التخصيصات التي يحتاج فى توجيهاتها الى الاعتبارات الركيكة و التكلفات الواهية فعلى هذا يجوز «شجرة سجدت» و «كوكب انقض الساعة وامثالهما ولا يجوز «رجل قائم» و نظائره
'His statement: that is, this is a preface: meaning that it is the predicate of a deleted subject, proceeding according to the principle in both subject and predicate. And among them are those who make it a deleted subject with the predicate deleted, i.e., the preface concerning the definition of logic, the need for it, and its subject matter. And it was objected to: that his statement 'a preface' is an indefinite noun, and it is not valid to predicate of it. And it was answered with several ways: among them, that it is specified by making the tanwin for glorification or belittlement, the first looking at the abundance of its benefits and the plenty of its returns, and the second at the fewness of its words and the conciseness of its expressions. And among them, that the deleted predicate is estimated before it, i.e., 'concerning the definition of logic, the need for it, and its subject matter is a preface', so it is analogous to your saying 'in the house is a man'. And among them, that this is based on what a group of verifiers mentioned, that the criterion for the validity of predicating an indefinite noun is benefit, not on what they mentioned of specifications that require, in their justifications, weak considerations and feeble contrivances. On this basis, 'a tree prostrated' and 'a star fell now' and the like are permissible, while 'a man standing' and its analogues are not permissible.'
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical and logical commentary on the opening statement of the text. The author (the commentator) explains that the word 'Mukaddimah' (preface) is functioning as the predicate (khabar) of a deleted subject (mubtada'), as per standard Arabic grammar. Some scholars instead treat it as a deleted subject with a deleted predicate. Then an objection is raised: the word 'Mukaddimah' is an indefinite noun (nakirah), which normally cannot serve as a predicate unless specified. The commentator provides three answers: first, the tanwin (nunation) indicates glorification (ta'zim) or belittlement (taqlil), making it specific enough. Second, the deleted predicate is placed before it, like 'in the house is a man', making it a quasi-sentence. Third, following a group of scholars, the criterion for predicating an indefinite noun is not specification but benefit (fa'idah) — if it provides new information, it is allowed. For example, 'a tree prostrated' is beneficial because it conveys a miracle, while 'a man standing' is not beneficial if the listener already knows men stand. This discussion is important for understanding how the author justifies the phrasing of the opening.

Checkpoint
According to the third answer, why is 'a tree prostrated' (شجرة سجدت) a permissible sentence?
A) Because 'tree' is specified by the tanwin for glorification.
B) Because it provides beneficial information about a miracle.
C) Because it is a metaphorical expression.
D) Because the predicate is deleted.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of an indefinite noun as a predicate hinges on whether it provides beneficial information (fa'idah), as argued by a group of verifiers in the commentary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the sentence 'kitabun mufid' (a beneficial book), determine which of the three justifications (tanwin specification, estimated predicate, or benefit criterion) allows it as a predicate. Provide a brief reasoning.
?
Provide an original Islamic science example where an indefinite noun is predicated and explain why it meets the benefit criterion. For instance, 'hadithun sahih' (a sound hadith) might be beneficial if the listener doesn't know its authenticity.
